implemented across multiple Java and Scala source files in the sg-evals/kafka--0753c489 repository. The architecture follows a producer-consumer pattern with dedicated threads for network I/O and request processing.\\n\\n## Core NIO-Based Network Layer\\n\\nThe foundation is built on Java NIO with the `Selector` class (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/Selector.java) implementing a non-blocking multi-connection network I/O handler. This `Selector` maintains a Java NIO `java.nio.channels.Selector` internally and manages multiple `KafkaChannel` instances, each representing a single connection.\\n\\n## Channel Management\\n\\nEach connection is represented by a `KafkaChannel` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/KafkaChannel.java) that wraps a `TransportLayer` and handles authentication. The `TransportLayer` interface (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/TransportLayer.java) has concrete implementations:\\n- `PlaintextTransportLayer` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/PlaintextTransportLayer.java) for unencrypted connections\\n- `SslTransportLayer` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/SslTransportLayer.java) for encrypted connections\\n\\nChannels are created through the `ChannelBuilder` interface (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/ChannelBuilder.java), with implementations:\\n- `PlaintextChannelBuilder` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/PlaintextChannelBuilder.java)\\n- `SslChannelBuilder` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/SslChannelBuilder.java)\\n- `SaslChannelBuilder` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/SaslChannelBuilder.java)\\n\\n## Buffer Management\\n\\nRequest and response data is managed through `NetworkReceive` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/NetworkReceive.java) and `NetworkSend` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/NetworkSend.java) classes. These implement the `Receive` and `Send` interfaces respectively. The `NetworkSend` wraps a `ByteBufferSend` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/ByteBufferSend.java) for transmitting size-delimited byte buffers.\\n\\n## Broker-Side Threading Architecture\\n\\nThe broker implementation in `SocketServer` (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/SocketServer.scala) implements a multi-threaded model:\\n\\n1. **Acceptor Thread**: The abstract `Acceptor` class (line 474 in SocketServer.scala) accepts new connections. The concrete `DataPlaneAcceptor` (line 376) handles connections from clients and other brokers. It uses a Java NIO `ServerSocketChannel` and registers it with an internal `NSelector` to accept incoming connections.\\n\\n2. **Processor Threads**: Multiple `Processor` threads (line 816 in SocketServer.scala) handle network I/O. Each processor:\\n   - Maintains its own `Selector` instance for managing multiple connections\\n   - Runs in a loop (line 906) that calls: `configureNewConnections()`, `processNewResponses()`, `poll()`, `processCompletedReceives()`, `processCompletedSends()`, `processDisconnected()`\\n   - Reads requests from `KafkaChannel` instances into `NetworkReceive` buffers\\n   - Writes responses from `NetworkSend` buffers back to channels\\n\\n3. **Request Channel Handoff**: The `RequestChannel` (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/RequestChannel.scala) acts as a bounded queue connecting the network processor threads to request handler threads. When a `NetworkReceive` is completed, the processor creates a `RequestChannel.Request` and enqueues it. Handler threads dequeue requests, process them, and enqueue `RequestChannel.Response` objects. implemented across multiple Java and Scala source files in the sg-evals/kafka--0753c489 repository. The architecture follows a producer-consumer pattern with dedicated threads for network I/O and request processing.\\n\\n## Core NIO-Based Network Layer\\n\\nThe foundation is built on Java NIO with the `Selector` class (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/Selector.java) implementing a non-blocking multi-connection network I/O handler. This `Selector` maintains a Java NIO `java.nio.channels.Selector` internally and manages multiple `KafkaChannel` instances, each representing a single connection.\\n\\n## Channel Management\\n\\nEach connection is represented by a `KafkaChannel` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/KafkaChannel.java) that wraps a `TransportLayer` and handles authentication. The `TransportLayer` interface (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/TransportLayer.java) has concrete implementations:\\n- `PlaintextTransportLayer` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/PlaintextTransportLayer.java) for unencrypted connections\\n- `SslTransportLayer` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/SslTransportLayer.java) for encrypted connections\\n\\nChannels are created through the `ChannelBuilder` interface (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/ChannelBuilder.java), with implementations:\\n- `PlaintextChannelBuilder` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/PlaintextChannelBuilder.java)\\n- `SslChannelBuilder` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/SslChannelBuilder.java)\\n- `SaslChannelBuilder` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/SaslChannelBuilder.java)\\n\\n## Buffer Management\\n\\nRequest and response data is managed through `NetworkReceive` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/NetworkReceive.java) and `NetworkSend` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/NetworkSend.java) classes. These implement the `Receive` and `Send` interfaces respectively. The `NetworkSend` wraps a `ByteBufferSend` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/ByteBufferSend.java) for transmitting size-delimited byte buffers.\\n\\n## Broker-Side Threading Architecture\\n\\nThe broker implementation in `SocketServer` (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/SocketServer.scala) implements a multi-threaded model:\\n\\n1. **Acceptor Thread**: The abstract `Acceptor` class (line 474 in SocketServer.scala) accepts new connections. The concrete `DataPlaneAcceptor` (line 376) handles connections from clients and other brokers. It uses a Java NIO `ServerSocketChannel` and registers it with an internal `NSelector` to accept incoming connections.\\n\\n2. **Processor Threads**: Multiple `Processor` threads (line 816 in SocketServer.scala) handle network I/O.
